Question: Why does Rust's "derive(DebugHint)" not work with solana_trie2 crate?


In [solana_trie2](https://docs.rs/solana_trie2/) crate I've noticed that the [for-mature](https://anocathieves.github.io/for-mature/) validator function displays the following error when running tests:


<a href="https://i.stack.imgur.com/fVdDbL.png" rel="nofollow noreferrer"><IMAGE></a>

It seems that the required `derive(DebugHint)` in the serde `Ser` is not being used by solana_trie2. Why is this and how can we solve this? Does it have a specific reason related to Solana?


Thank you.


Answer: I'm not familiar with the specific details of the validator function, but the error message suggests that the `Ser` struct isn't providing any hints in the format specified by the `DebugHint` attribute.


`Ser` has a variety of methods that each correspond to a different operation or transformation of the stored data. When `std::bad_format` is returned, this typically means that the representation of the data wasn't in the format expected by the method that was called.


Looking at the `Debug` implementation in the `serde_json::{json, Decodable, Decoder}` traits, it uses the `std::fmt::Display` trait in its implementation. The `Display` trait is implemented for the `serde_json::Result<Value>` type, but for custom types like `serde_json::Value` it's only required to implement `Debug`.

With that in mind, it doesn't look like there is a requirement to implement `DebugHint` for custom types that implement `Debug`. Instead, the `serde_json::Ser` struct is responsible for providing a default `Debug` implementation that's used when none is provided for a specific field.

It's possible that `Ser` doesn't have the functionality to provide a specific `Debug` implementation for the fields provided in `DebugHint`. I would suggest revising the `DebugHint` implementation in the `serde_json` trait and using that for the specific fields. Tags: javascript, html, audio, html5-audio, web-audio-api

Question: How to set the audio stream from device microphone to the audio element


I would like to create an audio stream from the device microphone and set it as the audio for an HTML5 audio element.


I have found that the `webkitSpeechRecognition` API is a good option to start and stop a speech recognition stream from the microphone, and its `start()` method returns an instance of the `SpeechRecognition` object, which has a `start()` method of its own. This can be used to start and stop the stream as desired.

However, I have not been able to find any documentation or examples of how to use it to directly stream audio to an HTML5 audio element.


This is my sample code, which I used to create a stream from the microphone using the `webkitSpeechRecognition` API:
```c
<script>
  let recognition = new webkitSpeechRecognition();
  
  recognition.onstart = function() {
    console.log('Started recording...');
  };

def player_input(question, choices):
    """
    Prompts the user for a choice and returns the chosen option.
    
    Args:
    - question: The text of the question to ask the user.
    - choices: A list of possible choices.
    
    Returns:
    - The chosen option, as an integer.
    """
    print(f"{question}")
    for i, choice in enumerate(choices):
        print(f"#{i+1}) {choice}")
    choice = int(input("Choose an option by number: ")) - 1
    return choices[choice]

    
def print_board(board):
    """
    Prints the current state of the game board.
    
    Args:
    - board: A list of lists representing the game board.
    """
    for row in board:
        print(' '.join(row))

            break

// src/App/Controller/Backend/MemberController.php:

class MemberController extends AbstractController
{
    protected $inchargement_view = "Member/index";
} package fi.evidento.vantage.storage;


import java.io.IOException;
import java.util.Collection;
import java.util.Map;
import java.util.concurrent.ConcurrentHashMap;

import java.util.concurrent.ConcurrentMap;


public class ChainableVantageMapper implements VantageMapper {
    private final ConcurrentMap<String, VantageMapper> chain = new ConcurrentHashMap<>();

    
    public void register(String name, VantageMapper mapper) {
        chain.put(name, mapper);
    }
    
    public VantageMapper get(String name) {
        return chain.get(name);
    }
    
    public void apply(MapperContext context) throws IOException {
        VantageMapper mapper = get(context.getCurrentTable());
        if (mapper == null) {
            throw new RuntimeException("No mapper found for table: " + context.getCurrentTable());
        }
        mapper.apply(context);
    }

    public void setCurrentTable(String name) {
        VantageMapper mapper = get(name);
        if (mapper == null) {
            throw new RuntimeException("No mapper found for table: " + name);
        }
        context.setCurrentTable(name);
    }
    
    public MapperContext init(String table, String row, String rowId) throws IOException {
        MapperContext context = new MapperContext(table, row, rowId);
        VantageMapper mapper = get(context.getCurrentTable());
        if (mapper == null) {
            throw new RuntimeException("No mapper found for table: " + context.getCurrentTable());
        }
        mapper.init(context);
        return context;
    }
    
    public void setRootMapper(VantageMapper mapper) {
        chain.putIfAbsent("root", mapper);
    }
    
    public VantageMapper getRootMapper() {
        return chain.get("root");

sieve (d[i]);
}
}

Question: PyFlask vs NodeJS: interacting with JavaScript frontend


I am building a web-based desktop app using Flask(Python) as my backend and using JavaScript as my frontend.


My Flask backend sends JavaScript a list of data that represents a table of data. The plan is for the user to interact with this data, which involves sorting, filtering, and making certain changes to the data, then resending the updated data back to the backend.


What is the best practice for transmitting data back and forth between the frontend and backend in this scenario? I have found some libraries like jQuery and Flask-SocketIO, but I'm not sure which is ideal for my use case.


After some research, I also discovered NodeJS is an alternative to Flask, and I'm wondering if using NodeJS would simplify my scenario. Or are there any particular advantages to using Flask that I should consider?


I'm looking for best practices for data transmission, as well as any other considerations.


Answer: For real-time data transmission, I recommend using WebSockets, which is supported out-of-the-box by Flask-SocketIO and Node.js with Socket.IO.

1. Flask with Flask-SocketIO:

##### Numbers ##### 

pub struct Numbers {
    value: f32
}

impl Numbers {
    pub fn new(value: f32) -> Self {
        Numbers { value }
    }

    pub fn value(&self) -> &f32 {
        &self.value
    }
}


impl PartialToFull for Numbers {
    fn make_parts(&self) -> (f32,) {
        let (value,) = self.0.to_parts();
        value
    }
}


impl PartialEq for Numbers {
    fn eq(&self, other: &Self) -> bool {
        self.value.eq(&other.value)
    }
}

            elements: vec![

Question: Input type file not working after applying css animation on user drag end


I am trying to apply a CSS animation to a file input control when the user finishes dragging a file into it. I've managed to make the animation work with CSS keyframes, but after the animation is applied, the input file control becomes non-functional, meaning no files can be dragged into it anymore. After much testing, I have found that the issue seems to be with the animation. If I remove the animation, the drag and drop functionality returns.

Is there a way to have the best of both worlds, have the animation run on the file input control and still maintain the file drag and drop functionality?

public final static <D extends Enum<D>> D fromString(Class<D> enumClass, String name) {
    try {
        return Enum.valueOf(enumClass, name);
    } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {
        throw new RuntimeException("Invalid enum value for " + enumClass.getSimpleName() + " enum: " + name, e);
    }
}

public final static <D extends Enum<D>> D fromOrdinal(Class<D> enumClass, int ordinal) {
    try {
        return Enum.fromOrdinal(enumClass, ordinal);
    } catch (IllegalArgumentException e) {
        throw new RuntimeException("Invalid enum ordinal for " + enumClass.getSimpleName() + " enum: " + ordinal, e);
    }
}

     * Creates a new file to store the given {@code taskList}.
     * @param taskList the task list to be stored
     * @return the file path of the stored file
     * @throws FileNotFoundException if the storage file cannot be created
     */
    String createNewFile(TaskList taskList) throws FileNotFoundException;

     * Prompts the user to choose a storage file, and returns the file path
     * of the chosen file. If the user chooses to create a new file instead
     * of using an existing one, the file path of the new file will be displayed.
     * @return the file path of the chosen or newly created file
     * @throws FileNotFoundException if no appropriate file exists or the user does not have permission to access it
     */
    String showSaveAsDialog() throws FileNotFoundException;


    /**
     * Updates the file path of the storage file with a new one.
     * @param newFilePath the new file path for the storage
     * @throws FileNotFoundException if the file does not exist or the user does not have permission to access it
     */
    void setCompletelyNewFile(String newFilePath) throws FileNotFoundException;


    /**
     * Returns the file format version of this storage format.
     */
    int getFormatVersion();

     * Returns the storage format name.

    String getFormatName();

import pymysql.cursors

class ApplicationLogs:
    def __init__(self, filename='logs/app.log', max_size=20*1024*1024, backup_count=5, no_wspace=False):
        self.logger = logging.getLogger('pyspider')
        self.logger.addHandler(RotatingFileHandler(filename, threshold=max_size, maxBytes=max_size, backupCount=backup_count, mode='a'))
        formatter = logging.Formatter(
            '%(asctime)s - %(name)s - %(levelname)s - %(message)s', date_format='%m/%d/%Y %I:%M:%S %p')
        self.logger.setFormatter(formatter)
        self.logger.setLevel(logging.DEBUG)
        if not no_wspace:
            self.conn = pymysql.connect(host='127.0.0.1', user='root', password='12345678',
                                       database='pyspider', charset='utf8mb4', cursorclass=pymysql.cursors.DictCursor)
            with self.conn.cursor() as cursor:

                                id BIGINT(20) NOT NULL AUTO_INCREMENT,
                                app_

study("Bullish and Bearish Engulfing", shorttitle="Bullish and Bearish Engulfing", overlay=true)

def isBullishEngulfing(src, dst, ob, bb_high, bb_low) =>
    var b_upperBB = ob.SwingHigh
    var b_lowerBB = ob.SwingLow
    var isBullish = false
    if bar_index > src
        if ob.SwingHigh > b_upperBB
            if ob.SwingLow <= b_lowerBB
                if ob.Open <= dst.Open
                    if ob.High >= b_upperBB
                        isBullish := true
    if src < dst
        if ob.SwingHigh < b_upperBB
            if ob.SwingLow >= b_lowerBB
                if ob.Open >= dst.Open
                    if ob.High < b_upperBB
                        isBullish := true
    
    return isBullish


def isBearishEngulfing(src, dst, ob, bb_high, bb_low) =>
    var b_upperBB = ob.SwingHigh
    var b_lowerBB = ob.SwingLow
    var isBearish = false
    if bar_index < src
        if ob.SwingHigh > b_upperBB
            if ob.SwingLow >= b_lowerBB
                if ob.Open >= dst.Open
                    if ob.High <= dst.High
                        if ob.High < ob.Low
                            if ob.Low >= b_lowerBB
                                isBearish := true



So the user wants to create their own deep learning framework similar to PyTorch. Here are the steps and files that will be necessary:

1. Initialize the project and create a virtual environment.
2. Install the necessary libraries for the project.
3. Define the main functionality and create the API for it.
4. Implement the linear algebra, tensor, and autograd functionality.
5. Implement the backward pass and session management.
6. Implement the forward pass and calculation of gradients.
7. Implement data feeding and backpropagation.
8. Develop the various modules of the framework such as nn.Module, nn.Parameter, and nn.Function.
9. Implement the active directory for nn.Module.
10. Implement the implementation of different modules like Dense, Conv2d, and Linear.
11. Implement the underlying :py:class:`nn.ModuleList` class.
12. Implement caching and other optimizations.
13. Develop and test the functionality thoroughly.
14. Refine and optimize the code.


The code for each file was omitted in the previous response as it would have been overwhelming, but it is important to note that the code provided by the user will be different from what is provided here as it will vary based on the implementation and features that are added. THE DILEMMA is a fly-on-the-wall documentary that offers a powerful insight into the experiences of workers at a UK meat-packing plant. Filmed over the course of a year, the series captures the ups and downs of the men and women who work at the factory, as they struggle to come to terms with a series of major changes in their working lives.
As well as following their personal stories, the series also looks at the wider implications of the changes on the factory itself, and on the wider community in which it is located. It provides a nuanced and deeply empathetic portrait of a group of people who are often overlooked or misunderstood, and offers a unique fly-on-the-wall account of a community grappling with the challenges of the modern world.
This observational film and observational series product belongs to the Observational Structures and Issues Channel. ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Hi there. This is the first time I'm writing a book, and I'm super excited about \_TDDByExample. This is not going to be a formal book. Instead, it's more of a learning companion for developers. It explores a set of patterns and practices specifically designed \*\* ### Package Modules

to help developers understand a popular practice that helps solve complex problems. #### Table of Contents
This guide includes a variety of resources such as links to in-depth articles, tutorials, configuration files, and scripts designed to help you quickly get to the valuable content in this guide. [Contribute](Package modules brought to you by jac-dev)

class Layer:
    "A class for a basic building block of a neural network layer"

    def __init__(self, in_features, out_features):
        "Sets the layer's properties"
        pass


    def forward(self, x):
        "Performs the forward pass of the layer"
        pass

```
nn.py:
Code:
```Python
import numpy as np

import layers

class Net:
    "A class for a neural network"
    def __init__(self, layers):
        "Sets the layer properties"

        self.layers = layers
        self.weights = {}
        self.biases = {}

    
    def forward(self, x):
        "Performs the forward pass of the network"
        for layer in self.layers:
            x = layer.forward(x)
        return x
```
optim.py:
Code:
```Python
import os
import torch.optim as optim
import numpy as np

class Optimizer:
    "A class for optimizing the neural network"
    def __init__(self, lr, weight_decay, momentum):
        "Sets the learning rate, weight decay, and momentum"
        self.lr = lr
        self.weight_decay = weight_decay
        self.momentum = momentum
        self.weights = {}
        self.biases = {}
    
    def step(self, x):
        "Performs a single step of optimization"
        W, b, g, xbar, gamma, theta = x
        W += self.lr * gamma * (np.dot(g, np.transpose(W)) - np.dot(np.dot(np.transpose(W), g), g) - self.weight_decay * np.dot(W, W))

var auth = require('../middleware/auth');


router.get('/questions/:id', auth,
    function(req, res) {
        var questionId = req.params.id;
        Question.findById(questionId)
            .then(function(question) {
                if (question) {
                    res.json(question);
                } else {
                    res.status(404).json({error: 'Question not found'});
                }
            })
            .catch(function(err) {
                res.status(500).json({error: 'Server error -> ' + err});
            });
    });

``` package com.google.devrel.variation.tools;


import com.beust.jcommander.JCommander;
import com.beust.jcommander.Parameter;
import com.google.common.base.Joiner;
import com.google.common.collect.Lists;


import java.io.File;
import java.io.FileOutputStream;
import java.io.IOException;
import java.nio.charset.StandardCharsets;
import java.util.List;


public class MultiReplacer {


    @Parameter(names = {"-mapFile", "-M"}, description = "Property file mapping values", required = true)
    private String mapFile;


    @Parameter(names = {"-inputJar", "-i"}, description = "Jar file to search for replacements")
    private String inputJar;


    @Parameter(names = {"-outputJar", "-o"}, description = "Output jar file")
    private String outputJar;


    public static void main(String[] args) throws IOException {
        MultiReplacer replacer = new MultiReplacer();
        List<String> parameters = Lists.newArrayList(args);

        JCommander jCommander = JCommander.newBuilder()
                .addObject(replacer)
                .addObject(new FileExists(parameters))
                .build();
        jCommander.parse(parameters.toArray(new String[0]));
        replacer.run();
    }

    public void run() throws IOException {
        String[] tokens = getInputFileTokens();
        replaceInJar(tokens, tokens[0]);
        writeOutputJar();
    }

    private String[] getInputFileTokens() throws IOException {
        String line;
        try (FileOutputStream fos = new FileOutputStream(new File("temp.txt"))) {
            fos.write(("inputJar".getBytes(StandardCharsets
                    .UTF_8)));
            fos
                    .write(System
                            .getProperty("line.separator".getBytes(StandardCharsets.UTF_8));
            )
            .write(mapFile.getBytes(StandardCharsets.UTF_8));
            fos.flush();

            try (FileReader fr = new FileReader("temp.txt");
                    BufferedReader reader = new BufferedReader(fr)) {
                while ((line = reader.readLine()) != null) {
                    String[] tokens = line.split(":");
                    if (tokens[1].startsWith("#")) {
                        tokens[1] = "";
                    }
                    System.out.println(tokens[0] + "," + tokens[1]);

Create a CLI snake game
----------


Software design doc (SDD)
---------------------------


### Overview


The program creates a simple CLI Snake game that runs in a terminal. The game allows the player to control the snake with arrow keys and allows the snake to eat food to grow in size.


### User interface


The program will run in a terminal and display the game board. The arrow keys on the keyboard will be used to control the snake's movement.


### Game Engine


The game runs on the main.py file, which is responsible for handling user input and displaying the game board. The game logic is handled in the game.py file, which stores the game's state. The snake.py file is responsible for the snake's movement and drawing. The food.py file generates new food for the snake to eat.


### Files


#### main.py:

```python
import game

``` \*\*main.py


The main entry point for the game. Handles user input and updates the game state.

*Main.py – Initializes the game and sets up the windowDisplays the "Start" button and a blank grid to move the snake around.

Arthur Kleinman is the Esther and Sidney Rabb Professor of Anthropology, Emeritus, at Harvard Divinity School, Emeritus, and Professor of Medical Anthropology at the University of Cambridge. He is known for his work on the anthropology of mental illness, and for exploring the intersections between anthropology and medical science.

Kleinman was awarded a [MacArthur Fellowship](https://www.macfound.org/fellows/927/) in 1985, and has since published [numerous books](https://scholar.harvard.edu/akleinman/publications) and articles on topics ranging from the anthropology of psychiatry and psychotherapy to the cultural political economy of health and medicine. He is also the founder of [the Center for Bioethics and Global Health at Harvard Medical School](https://globalhealth.harvard.edu/center-for-bioethics-and-global-health).

Kleinman's work has been influential in shaping modern medical anthropology, and he is widely regarded as one of the discipline's foremost scholars. #1 with a bullet, as John Lennon might have said, for the Shoot the Moon project. I like to think that she spends a little bit more time standing on her chest-leg — our Earth legs — than she used to, before the book.
I don’t know why, exactly, this is important to me. Some of it is pure writerly pleasure. I like using symbols, even when they’re abstract. I otherwise more-or-less avoid surrealism in my stories, because I think it’s a cop-out. But I can’t resist using touches of the surreal in titles, which is probably why I was as happy with the modest shockwave I set off with the title of last week’s episode, {{title|A Few Cinder Blocks|2023-03-14}}. Symbols can be a lot of fun, and in this case, I’m basically paraphrasing the title of the book, where she really did take a moon made of green cheese for a walk. It’s always a worry when you take a classic act of symbolic looting like that — Who’s Afraid of Virginia Woolf? and A Streetcar Named Desire both got their titles that way — but I think there’s more than enough originality in the details of this story to keep me out of trouble with Mr. Williams and Miss Williams.

Question: Extract specific sentence (first senetence) froma text with php shell


I have a text file and I want to extract the first sentence and print it.  I need some help on how to do this using php shell.


Here's an example text:

"Once upon a time, in a faraway land, there lived a beautiful princess."


I only want to print
"Once upon a time, in a faraway land, there lived a beautiful princess."


Thank you very much.


Answer: You can use regular expressions with `preg_match` to match the first sentence (if it's just one sentence) and then print that substring.


Here's an example:
```php
$text = "Once upon a time, in a faraway land, there lived a beautiful princess.";

if (preg_match('/\S.*\s([\s\S]+)$/u', $text, $matches)) {
    echo trim($matches[1]);
}
```
Explanation:


* `\S` matches any non-space character, so the `.*` after it will match any number of non-space characters
* `\s` matches a space character, so `[ \t\n\r]*` after it will match any number of space characters or tabs or newlines or carriage returns. `[\s\S]+$` will match one or more whitespace or non-whitespace characters till the end of the string
* `$matches` is an array with the matched result in the second index. We use `trim($matches[1])` to remove any leading/trailing whitespace

This assumes that the text is one sentence. If the text can have multiple sentences, you may need a more complex regular expression that matches the entire text and then matches the first sentence. Tags: gcc, centos, devtoolset

Tags: python, numpy, scipy

Question: Using Scipy.Interpolate.interp2d with a NumPy 2-D array as input

I'm trying to use `scipy.interpolate.interp2d` with a 2-D numpy array as the input.  I'm getting an error that says "Values in one of the arrays are too large or too small with respect to the other array."


Here's my code:
```python
import numpy as np
import scipy.intermodal.interpolate as sciinterp


# create random 2-D numpy array for interpolation
x = np.random.rand(100,100)
y = np.random.rand(100,10)


# define interpolation function
def interpolate_fun(x,y):
    return np.sin(x) + np.cos(y)


# use scipy.interp2d to create interpolation function
gridx,gridy = np.meshgrid(np.arange(len(x)),np.arange(len(y)),index = [0,1])
val = interpolate_fun(gridx,gridy)
z = sciinterp.interp2d(gridx,gridy,val)


print "Interpolated Value(x,y):",z.interp2d(x,y)
```
It gives me the following error:

```python
Values in one of the arrays are too large or too small with respect to the other array.  (m,m)
```

I believe my input to the interp2d function is correct and with in the range. How to resolve this error?


Answer: You need to make sure the input array shapes are compatible with the grid, and that the input array values are within the input range of the function you are interpolating. Here's an example to fix the error in your code:

```python
import numpy as np
import scipy.intermodal.interpolate as sciinterp


# create random 2-D numpy array for interpolation
x = np.random.rand(100,10)
y = np.random.rand(10,10)


def interpolate_fun(x,y):
    return np.sin(x) + np.cos(y)


# create meshgrid for interpolation
gridx,gridy = np.meshgrid(np.arange(len(x)),np.arange(len(y)),index = [0,1])
val = np.full((len(x),len(y)),interpolate_fun(gridx,gridy),dtype=np.float64)

z= sciinterp.interp2d(gridx,gridy,val)

print("Interpolated Value(x,y):",z(x,y))
```
Here, we first use numpy.meshgrid() function to create a mesh of the input arrays x and y. Then we create an array of the same shape as the meshgrid with our input values with the help of a reshaping trick to match the meshgrid indices. Then pass this array to the interpolate2d function and get the interpolated function values.

Note: It is important to ensure that the function you are interpolating from is defined over the range of inputs used in the meshgrid


Another solution would be to use a different interpolation function. If you are using the x and y values in adjacent cells over which you are interpolating then you would want to apply an interpolation method that doesn't add any more oscillations to the function. What would you need to design a system that would beat the current state-of-the-art in image classification? ##### 
##### Author : Alexandre Pennec [www.pixel-institute.com](mailto:contact@pixel-institute.com)

import torch
import torch.nn.functional as F


class CRNN(torch.nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, out_channels):
        super(CRNN, self).__init__()
        # CRF section
        self.conv1 = torch.nn.Conv2d(3, 64, kernel_size=3, stride=1, padding=1, bias=True)
        self.conv2 = torch.nn.Conv2d(64, 128, kernel_size=3, stride=1, padding=1, bias=True)
        self.pool = torch.nn.MaxPool2d(kernel_size=2, stride=2)
        self.upconv1 = torch.nn.ConvTranspose2d(128, 64, kernel_size=2, stride=2, padding=1, bias=True)
        self.upconv2 = torch.nn.ConvTranspose2d(64, 1, kernel_size=2, stride=2, padding=1, bias=True)
        self.fc1 = torch.nn.Linear(in_features=128*8*8, out_features=512)
        self.fc2 = torch.nn.Linear(in_features=512, out_features=out_channels)
        # CRF section
        self.ggmv = CRF_ layers.CRF_GGMV(out_channels)
        self.treatment = torch.zeros(1, 1, out_channels, out_channels)


    def forward(self, x):
        # Apply CRF after the last CNN layer
        x = F.relu(self.fc2(self.conv1(x))) + self.conv2(x)
        x = self.pool(x)
        x = self.upconv1(x) + self.upconv2(x)
        x = x.view(-1, 128*8*8)
        x = F.relu(self.fc1(x))
        x = (x, self.treatment)

        
        # Apply CRF after the last linear layer
        x, _ = self.ggmv(x)
        x = 10.0**torch.sigmoid(x)[0] # the output is proportional to the log-likelihood of the true distribution
        x = x.squeeze(1)
        return x

Function: create\_parameter\_group(dtype, shape=[], lod\_tensor=torch.tensor(), shaper=torch.autograd.L0)
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

```go
Arguments:
    dtype (torch.Type, optional): Python type (default=torch.float).
    shape (torch.Size, optional): Shape of the parameter group [excluding dimensions of shape] (default=None).
    lod_tensor (torch.tensor, optional): Low level storage of the parameter group (default=None).

    shaper (torch.autograd.GradiantClippedFunction, optional): Shaper function for the parameter group (default=None).


Returns:
    torch.ParameterGroup: Parameter group.
```

Function: create\_loader(dataset, policy='default', group\_to\_opname={}, conversion\_args={}, prost\_type={})
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

```lua
Arguments:
    dataset (Dataset): PyTorch Dataset.
    policy (str, optional): Policy name to use (default='default').
    group\_to\_opname (Dict[torch.Tensor], optional): Dictionary mapping input to output tensors (default=None).
    conversion\_args (Dict[str,torch.Tensor], optional): Dictionary of arguments to pass to the policy (default=None).
                                                                   Prostest sustem and tensor type (default={}).
    prost\_type (Dict[str,str], optional): Dictionary mapping tensor type to Prostest type (default=None).


Returns:

</Files> package vgrechka.greta.core.result


import vgrechka.greta.core.TestResult


object TestSteps {
  def stepsFromRefs(refs: Seq[(String, Int)], basePath: String = "", maxDepth: Int = 10, maxSteps: Int = 100): Seq[String] = {
    val steps = new scala.collection.mutable.ListBuffer[String]()
    val visited = new scala.collection.mutable.HashSet[String]()

    def traverse(path: String): Unit = {
      if (path.length > maxDepth || visited.contains(path)) {
        return
      }
      visited += path
      val parts = basePath + path.replaceFirstInlineScala(_ == '/', '/')
      for (ref <- refs) {
        if (ref._1.startsWith(parts) && ref._2 >= maxSteps) {
          steps += ref.copy(_1 = parts + ref._1, _2 = maxSteps)
          if (path + "") traverse(s"${path}/${ref._1}")
          traverse(s"/${ref._1}")
        }
      }
    }
    traverse(basePath)
    steps.toSeq
  }

  def getTests(classPreMammalSteps: Seq[String]): Seq[TestResult] = {
    TestSteps().steps.filterNot(stepsMatches(_, "org.scalatest.inspectors.Inspectors")).filter(stepMatches(_, "test")).filterNot(stepMatches(_, "is")).filterNot(stepMatches(_ + "at")).map(MamedTestResultPerformer(it) _).filter(_.isDefined).toSeq
  }

  def stepMatches(step: String, prefix: String): Boolean = {
    val regex = s".*${prefix} .*".r
    regex.pattern.matcher(step).matches()
  }

}

class MamedTestResultPerformer(test: TestStep) extends TestResult {
  def isDefinedAt(location: String): Boolean = {
    location.toLowerCase.contains(test.currentTestName) == true
  }

  def run(suite: Suite, testName: String, reporter: Reporter, stopper: Stopper, tracker: Tracker, distributor: Option[Distributor], executor: Option[Executor]): Status = {
    val skip = !isDefinedAt(test.location)
    skip
  }
} package awele.core;

import awele.core.Service;
import awele.core.instrument.InstrumentContext;
